    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me a question starting with "ME:", so I need to answer with "ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is: "Does the questioner know what is in the southwest? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the conversation history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner previously asked: "QUESTIONER: What is in the southwest?"} \\
\texttt{{-} I answered: "ANSWER: wrench"} \\
\texttt{{-} So the questioner has been told that wrench is in the southwest.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Therefore, the questioner does know what is in the southwest.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The user wants me to answer with yes or no and then stop. But the format requires "ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I should answer: "ASIDE: Yes." or "ASIDE: Yes, the questioner knows that wrench is in the southwest."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But the user specifically said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." This seems to conflict slightly with the "ASIDE: <one sentence>" format, but I should follow the primary format instruction which says "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: "ASIDE: Yes."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or I could say: "ASIDE: Yes, the questioner was told that wrench is in the southwest."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But since the user said "with yes or no and then stop", probably just "ASIDE: Yes." is best.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, let me check if there's any trick here. The setup says "Things are in different places, but the questioner does not know about it yet." But then the questioner asked "What is in the southwest?" and I told them "wrench". So now they do know.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the answer is yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Format: ASIDE: Yes. </think> ASIDE: Yes.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\
